  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129114032?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elisa Rolle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elisa Rolle" href="/user/show/2156728-elisa-rolle">Elisa Rolle</a>

          added it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129114032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6614087229189155961">Homosexuality and christianity are two concepts that is no easy to put in the same sentence without them being at the opposite. <br/><br/>Paul is the perfect teenager: a beloved son, an attentive boyfriend, a good friend, he is perfect in anything he wants to achieve. But I felt something uneasy in Paul, a drive to be accepted that is almost unhealthy: Paul is a latino american, but when he moved to Texas with his parents, he was the odd kid out and the only to accept him was Angie, a kid his same age who</span>
  <span id="freeText6614087229189155961" style="display:none">Homosexuality and christianity are two concepts that is no easy to put in the same sentence without them being at the opposite. <br /><br />Paul is the perfect teenager: a beloved son, an attentive boyfriend, a good friend, he is perfect in anything he wants to achieve. But I felt something uneasy in Paul, a drive to be accepted that is almost unhealthy: Paul is a latino american, but when he moved to Texas with his parents, he was the odd kid out and the only to accept him was Angie, a kid his same age who was beautiful and kind, and very religious. Angie is the good kind of religious girl, the type who really understands the concept of “love your neighbor as yourself”. In the little child Paolo, the concept to be accept was similar to the concept be like Angie, if he was like Angie he would be part of a group. And so little Paolo became Paul, and he also became a good Christian boy, every Sunday in the church, and of course he became also Angie’s boyfriend. To excel in everything was for Paul a proof that he was one of them, one of the good boy. <br /><br />When he is a teenager, Paul starts to have “strange” feelings for other guys, feelings that Paul is more than able to indentify, but that he doesn’t want to acknowledge: being gay means being not perfect, it’s against the religion he was taught, it’s against the life he is expecting to have, it’s, above all, against his feelings for Angie, being gay means that he has to leave Angie, and leaving Angie is something he doesn’t want to consider, Angie represents everything little Paolo wanted. <br /><br />When Manuel, an out and proud gay guy, transfer to their school, it’s not the first time Paul was questioning his sexuality. It’s not fault, or merit, of Manuel that Paul realizes he is gay, Manuel is only giving to Paul the proof that there is another way to consider the question, being gay doesn’t mean being excluded, being unhappy, being a paria. Manuel is not hiding his feelings, and moreover, he is not denying his love for Jesus Christ and God; Manuel achieved the result of accepting himself and at the same time continuing to love God and religion, only that his concept of God and religion is a concept of love and acceptance, not a concept of refusal and limitation. <br /><br />Paul and Manuel’s path is not easy, and they will have a chance only since, among the majority of people who will refuse them, they will find also people who will accept them, not since those people are good or kind, but simply since those people will understand that Paul and Manuel are like any other teenager. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com/dp/1416909001/?tag=elimyrevandra-20">http://www.amazon.com/dp/1416909001/?...</a></span>

<div id="review_267986815" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267986815" />
    <a title="Brandy Shark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4764366-brandy-shark"><img alt="Brandy Shark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442634364p2/4764366.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandy Shark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandy Shark" href="/user/show/4764366-brandy-shark">Brandy Shark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">gay teenagers, gay christians, those who support gay rights</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4764366-brandy-shark?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4764366-brandy-shark?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer267986815&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267986815" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2608536620065701257">There were things I loved about this book, and then things that I didn't care for (but that mostly revolved around under developed secondary characters, and pace and voice), but I decided to give the book a four star rating because at the core of it, it really made me think, as well as touch me.<br/><br/>Overall, the writing was kind of slack, nothing real special about it, but I could completely relate to the story. I went to high school in a rural area, and a very closed-minded one at that. While I was </span>
  <span id="freeText2608536620065701257" style="display:none">There were things I loved about this book, and then things that I didn't care for (but that mostly revolved around under developed secondary characters, and pace and voice), but I decided to give the book a four star rating because at the core of it, it really made me think, as well as touch me.<br /><br />Overall, the writing was kind of slack, nothing real special about it, but I could completely relate to the story. I went to high school in a rural area, and a very closed-minded one at that. While I was in school there were only three openly gay students, and some of us tried to start a GSA club, which was approved by administration, but other students tried to block it, citing it was against their religion. And that hurt me. Because, I'm a Christian, but I don't believe being gay is wrong; you're born that way.<br /><br />I loved Manuel and how he always fought the bigotry and narrow-mindedness with actual quotes from scripture. Not very often you see in the media (books, film, or television) where a character is both gay, and Christian, because I know there are many gay Christians in this country. I was also very happy that Angie and Dakota were the head starters behind the GSA, and how open and loving they were to Manuel, as well as Paul. <br /><br />I knew people in high school who were like Cliff and Elizabeth, so narrow minded when it came to the subject of homosexuality that they seemed to be missing the complete point of God and Jesus, and would never ever consider looking at scripture in a different light, other than what is actually on the paper. If you believed differently, then you were wrong. I knew a girl in school when she found out that one of our friends was gay, she started crying because she thought he was going to Hell.<br /><br />There are a lot elements that I was glad were brought into the story, like the Pastor (who disgusted me) and the whole ex-gay crusade which is sadly going strong today. I loved Abuela, everything about her. And I loved that Paul's father was accepting.<br /><br />There were some plot points that were kind of trite and predictable, and the writing wasn't that strong, but I couldn't but down the book. It touched me on a very personal level and I think all teenagers who are conflicted about their faith and sexuality should read this book.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1268486221" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1268486221" />
    <a title="Gene Hult" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3989343-gene-hult"><img alt="Gene Hult" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531495776p2/3989343.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1268486221?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gene Hult" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gene Hult" href="/user/show/3989343-gene-hult">Gene Hult</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416909002" href="/book/show/6560612-the-god-box">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1268486221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8517157994740503149">Although I've read and enjoyed most of his books now, Alex Sanchez isn't technically a great writer. His prose is sometimes awkward and sounds like it was translated. He's over-earnest, sometimes transparently manipulative with his pat characters, and incredibly preachy and didactic. In parts, his writing can read like a social worker's case files. So why do I love his books so much?<br/><br/>I will read anything Sanchez writes because his books have enormous heart. They brim with emotion, hope, and goodn</span>
  <span id="freeText8517157994740503149" style="display:none">Although I've read and enjoyed most of his books now, Alex Sanchez isn't technically a great writer. His prose is sometimes awkward and sounds like it was translated. He's over-earnest, sometimes transparently manipulative with his pat characters, and incredibly preachy and didactic. In parts, his writing can read like a social worker's case files. So why do I love his books so much?<br /><br />I will read anything Sanchez writes because his books have enormous heart. They brim with emotion, hope, and goodness. Usually, he makes me start crying about halfway through, and then I must finish the rest of the book through constant trickling tears. Which can get quite blurry! He cares so much for his characters, and they act in such lovely ways, that I'm a wreck. Plus I'm oversensitive about teen gay issues anyway, given how hard it was to live through those years, so his honest, direct, supportive, sweet, and heartfelt approach turns me into a puddle every time.<br /><br /><i>The God Box</i> was no different. He's deepened some of his characterizations, but the prose still reads just so slightly off-rhythm, and there are huge passages of researched Bible quotes about homosexuality discussed in long presentations of questions. These are obviously planted by the author relatively inorganically, and also fascinating, and would give any young LGBT teen great information to battle the hate spewed in the erroneous name of faith and religion . . . without suggesting any kind of rejection of God or faith or spirituality. So that's extremely useful and so helpful that it seems mean-spirited to carp about the storytelling. Especially when the love for the characters overwhelms you halfway through and makes you shake with sobs. Not entirely sad sobs, either! Happy weeping, in joy and recognition and understanding.<br /><br />So read Alex Sanchez. Read <i>The God Box</i>. It's an important, beautiful book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8517157994740503149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1187072943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1187072943" />
    <a title="Menglong Youk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27195238-menglong-youk"><img alt="Menglong Youk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545907056p2/27195238.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1187072943?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Menglong Youk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Menglong Youk" href="/user/show/27195238-menglong-youk">Menglong Youk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27195238-menglong-youk?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27195238-menglong-youk?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27195238-menglong-youk?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27195238-menglong-youk?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27195238-menglong-youk?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1187072943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4219506063464371716">4.5 stars<br/><br/>Paul and Angie have been dating since they were in middle school; they wholeheartedly love each other, dating regularly, kissing, talking on phone and having fun just like normal couples. However, something is weird about Paul; he feels like Angie isn't sexually attracted to him at all. Anyway, Paul is Christian, reading and quoting lines in the Bible and joining a club discussing Christianity. He strongly believes that homosexuality is a sin. In the start of his school year, a new stud</span>
  <span id="freeText4219506063464371716" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />Paul and Angie have been dating since they were in middle school; they wholeheartedly love each other, dating regularly, kissing, talking on phone and having fun just like normal couples. However, something is weird about Paul; he feels like Angie isn't sexually attracted to him at all. Anyway, Paul is Christian, reading and quoting lines in the Bible and joining a club discussing Christianity. He strongly believes that homosexuality is a sin. In the start of his school year, a new student, Samuel, registered in his school and joined lunch table with him and his friends. During the talk, Samuel announces that he's gay. This makes Paul shock and feel uncomfortable about being with Samuel. As the story develops, we can see that Paul's religious perspective starts being adjusted, but he has to face many obstacles awaiting for him.<br /><br />This is the last book of Alex Sanchez's that I've read. Honestly speaking, if it wasn't for Alex Sanchez being the author of this book, I perhaps wouldn't pick it up and read at the first place. I spent my afternoon finishing reading this book in awe. Well, I'm an atheist, so homosexuality isn't a concerned matter for me. Why are people sent to hell just because they love somebody? That's completely absurd. Love isn't about gander, it's about two soul uniting and being pleased with each other. On the 4/5 throught the the book, I was going to give it only 4 stars, but when I finished reading the last part, I couldn't stop myself from giving it 0.5 stars more. This book is highly recommended, especially for Christians. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4219506063464371716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13121057631465277205" style="display:none">I almost put this book down. I thought I had accidently grabbed some Christian literature…which I seldom read. Too preachy and I don’t need my shortcomings pointed out in a book, thank you very much. That’s why I have a mother.<br /><br />There is more scripture quoted in this book than a church pamphlet on Sunday morning. Manual is a newcomer to an ultra-conservative school and openly admits he is gay. The majority of his classmates, as well as many teachers, are just as openly anti-gay. Both sides are using THE WORD to make their point. It was like reading about a long tennis match…which is only slightly more boring that watching a long tennis match. <br /><br />Several things saved the book:<br />*The content. This is teen fiction and addresses some important issues: tolerance, identity, hate, etc.<br /><br />*The writing. The author writes with compassion. I imagine he has quite a following with younger readers.<br /><br />*The zingers.<br />	“Sex and religion don’t mix,” my grandma once told me. “The church should stay out of people’s pants.”<br /><br />And…<br /><br />	Elizabeth braced herself on the table. “You mean you’re a practicing homosexual?”<br />Manuel studied her a moment, as if debating whether to take her question seriously. “Well, actually, I think I’ve got the hang of it by now.”<br /><br />4 big stars.<br /><br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phil Ansell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil Ansell" href="/user/show/5612096-phil-ansell">Phil Ansell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10054380-the-god-box">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5612096-phil-ansell?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5612096-phil-ansell?shelf=m-m-romance">m-m-romance</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer213808722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9851198437205500633">Fantastic!! Alex Sanchez tells a touching story of Paul, a Christian teenager who is really struggling with his confusing and developing homosexual feelings. His world is opened and challenged when he meets out and proud teenager Manuel.<br/><br/>The story is brilliant and wonderfully written but what I absolutely loved was how Alex Sanchez addressed and challenged pretty much every Bible passage that appears to condemn homosexuality, and especially those that the Church and certain Christian groups use a</span>
  <span id="freeText9851198437205500633" style="display:none">Fantastic!! Alex Sanchez tells a touching story of Paul, a Christian teenager who is really struggling with his confusing and developing homosexual feelings. His world is opened and challenged when he meets out and proud teenager Manuel.<br /><br />The story is brilliant and wonderfully written but what I absolutely loved was how Alex Sanchez addressed and challenged pretty much every Bible passage that appears to condemn homosexuality, and especially those that the Church and certain Christian groups use against gay people. I fully believe that every Christian needs to read this book! It gives you a full sense of what it means to be loving and accepting, exactly what Jesus wants us to be. <br /><br />Anyone who is, or has, ever struggled with coming out or accepting themselves for who they are then this book shows you that you are certainly not alone and gives a wonderful message of hope.<br />If you are struggling with being gay and Christian then don't hesitate to pick it up.<br /><br />I personally got a lot out of this book both academically and spiritually, and in terms of entertainment it was engaging and moving. I absolutely loved it. Thank you Alex Sanchez for writing this, I will certainly be checking out more of your books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9851198437205500633" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23485243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6037681889099307577"> I was initially afraid that these characters would sound the same as the ones in the Rainbow Boys series, but luckily I was wrong. The story still had a unique voice, despite covering familiar ground: coming out, high school, and family issues. The major issue that this book tackles in a pretty great way is homosexuality and the bible. Tough topic, right? I know!<br/> I wish I was much more familiar with the bible so I could form my own opinions on what the big book has to say on the issues the char</span>
  <span id="freeText6037681889099307577" style="display:none"> I was initially afraid that these characters would sound the same as the ones in the Rainbow Boys series, but luckily I was wrong. The story still had a unique voice, despite covering familiar ground: coming out, high school, and family issues. The major issue that this book tackles in a pretty great way is homosexuality and the bible. Tough topic, right? I know!<br /> I wish I was much more familiar with the bible so I could form my own opinions on what the big book has to say on the issues the characters discuss, but it wasn't necessary to follow the story. Wow, that sentence was too long. What I found really stupendous(or maybe even, tremendous? Eh, why not?) was how the characters presented the bible excerpts. First, they discussed how those excerpts were traditionally interpreted and then one of the main characters would refute their ideas by giving them a new perspective that made more sense. <br /> Overall, the characters were likeable and the story has a good pace. Sanchez is always good at portraying inner(does a hyphen belong here?) turmoil that makes it really easy to sympathize and become invested in the characters. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6037681889099307577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30908941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9745196941922471904">Hispanic Jesus lover Paul had always prayed that God would take his gay feelings away so he could love his girlfriend Angie like a "normal" red-blooded Texas high school student. This all starts to change with the arrival of Manuel, a cute and openly gay boy from Dallas who also happens to be Christian and extremely good at explaining how the scripture's condemnations of homosexuality are not actually legitimate reasons for people to hate gay people. Manuel's winning personality and powers of pe</span>
  <span id="freeText9745196941922471904" style="display:none">Hispanic Jesus lover Paul had always prayed that God would take his gay feelings away so he could love his girlfriend Angie like a "normal" red-blooded Texas high school student. This all starts to change with the arrival of Manuel, a cute and openly gay boy from Dallas who also happens to be Christian and extremely good at explaining how the scripture's condemnations of homosexuality are not actually legitimate reasons for people to hate gay people. Manuel's winning personality and powers of persuasion don't convince everybody, however. A rift begins to grow in the school, and Paul is forced to face his worst fears.<br /><br />A plain, straightforward first person narrative with somewhat unrealistic characters (especially Manuel, the magical gay boy who arrives to make everything better), but I still liked it and rooted for people. Without knowing much about the Bible, I will go ahead and say that the scriptural analysis sounded pretty convincing, so it'd probably be a good recommendation for kids who are worried that God hates them for being gay.<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Travis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Travis" href="/user/show/4761577-travis">Travis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4761577-travis?shelf=2009">2009</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138826197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12650961281413307824">Paul is a Christian teen who has been dating his best friend Angie since middle school, but while he loves her, he feels no attraction towards her. Every night he prays that God will make him attracted to girls and take away his feelings about guys. Then he meets Manuel, who is a Christian and gay and sees nothing contradictory about that. As Paul and Manuel become closer, he starts to question what he's been taught about the evils of homosexuality.[return][return]I won't lie. This book is as su</span>
  <span id="freeText12650961281413307824" style="display:none">Paul is a Christian teen who has been dating his best friend Angie since middle school, but while he loves her, he feels no attraction towards her. Every night he prays that God will make him attracted to girls and take away his feelings about guys. Then he meets Manuel, who is a Christian and gay and sees nothing contradictory about that. As Paul and Manuel become closer, he starts to question what he's been taught about the evils of homosexuality.[return][return]I won't lie. This book is as subtle as a brick and Manuel is unbelievably wise and perfect for a teenager, but I loved it to death. I don't really consider myself a Christian anymore (and I was never this sort of actively-Christian Christian myself), but this is how I grew up and Sanchez portrays the conservative Christian community perfectly. Reading this felt so familiar to me. The Christians in this book aren't parodies; they're real people, and I loved that the story wasn't about choosing between being a Christian and being gay, but about being a gay Christian.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g4YKI2qxUgjPzSEmhW/Uv+LE+mhlomaZL5LRloFEbKWoImsl4MA28TteGs7STbLDNtjyqKus2Sk2mk6LowZz2Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yP2lpxm63C76BCTyJoLCEM0/DY3If2CsuIUL89f2P1fjWcShk8u41w6XHxpxoKRsGSMFTQZx3xyhjZTu9bQgKw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5474146175323134830">Alex Sanchez is the author of the Rainbow Boys trilogy of teen novels, along with The God Box, Getting It, and the Lambda Award-winning middle-grade novel So Hard to Say. His novel, Bait, won the Florida Book Award Gold Medal for YA fiction. Alex received his master’s degree in guidance and counseling from Old Dominion University and for many years worked as a youth and family counselor. His newes</span>
  <span id="freeText5474146175323134830" style="display:none">Alex Sanchez is the author of the Rainbow Boys trilogy of teen novels, along with The God Box, Getting It, and the Lambda Award-winning middle-grade novel So Hard to Say. His novel, Bait, won the Florida Book Award Gold Medal for YA fiction. Alex received his master’s degree in guidance and counseling from Old Dominion University and for many years worked as a youth and family counselor. His newest book is a graphic novel from DC Comics, You Brought Me the Ocean. Find out more about Alex at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.AlexSanchez.com">www.AlexSanchez.com</a></span>
